<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#CCF; font-weight:bold;">Anime</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#EEF; font-weight:normal;"><i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Resurrection</i></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Studio</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Sunrise_(company)" title="Sunrise (company)">Sunrise</a></td>
</tr>
<tr class="noprint">
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#CCF; font-weight:bold"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikipe-tan_face.svg"><img alt="Wikipe-tan face.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="440" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wikipe-tan_face.svg/16px-Wikipe-tan_face.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wikipe-tan_face.svg/24px-Wikipe-tan_face.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wikipe-tan_face.svg/32px-Wikipe-tan_face.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portal:Anime_and_Manga" title="Portal:Anime and Manga">Anime and Manga portal</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i><b>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion</b></i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反逆のルルーシュ</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Hangyaku no Rurūshu</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, often referred to as simply <i>Code Geass</i>, is a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> <a href="/wiki/Television_program" title="Television program">series</a> created by <a href="/wiki/Sunrise_(company)" title="Sunrise (company)">Sunrise</a>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Gor%C5%8D_Taniguchi" title="Gorō Taniguchi">Gorō Taniguchi</a>, and written by <a href="/wiki/Ichir%C5%8D_%C5%8Ckouchi" title="Ichirō Ōkouchi">Ichirō Ōkouchi</a>, with original character designs by manga authors <a href="/wiki/Clamp_(manga_artists)" title="Clamp (manga artists)">Clamp</a>. Set in an <a href="/wiki/Alternate_history" title="Alternate history">alternate timeline</a>, the series focuses on how the former prince <a href="/wiki/Lelouch_Lamperouge" title="Lelouch Lamperouge">Lelouch vi Britannia</a> obtains a power known as Geass and decides to use it to obliterate the Holy Britannian Empire, a <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a> that has been conquering various countries.</p>
<p><i>Code Geass</i> first ran in Japan on <a href="/wiki/Mainichi_Broadcasting_System" title="Mainichi Broadcasting System">MBS</a> from October 5, 2006, to July 28, 2007. Its sequel series, <i><b>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion R2</b></i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反逆のルルーシュR2</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu Hangyaku no Rurūshu Āru Tsū</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, ran as a simulcast on <a href="/wiki/Japan_News_Network" title="Japan News Network">JNN</a> stations (like MBS and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Broadcasting_System" title="Tokyo Broadcasting System">TBS</a>) from April 6, 2008 to September 28, 2008. The series has also been adapted into various <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Light_novel" title="Light novel">light novels</a> with the former showing various alternate scenarios from the TV series. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bandai_Entertainment" title="Bandai Entertainment">Bandai Entertainment</a> also licensed most parts from the franchise for English release in December 2007, airing the two TV series on <a href="/wiki/Adult_Swim" title="Adult Swim">Adult Swim</a>. Most manga and light novels have also been published in North America by Bandai. At the Code Geass 10th anniversary event on November 27, 2016, it was announced that the series will be receiving a new anime, along with a compilation film trilogy in 2017 that will recap the events from both seasons of the anime series. The new anime, titled <i><b>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Resurrection</b></i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス　復活のルルーシュ</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Fukkatsu no Rurūshu</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, will take place a few years after the events of Zero Requiem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The director <a href="/wiki/Gor%C5%8D_Taniguchi" title="Gorō Taniguchi">Gorō Taniguchi</a> commented that the upcoming project would star an alive Lelouch and not as an alternate setting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Released to critical acclaim, the TV anime series has been well received in Japan, selling over a million DVD and Blu-ray Disc volumes. Both seasons have won several awards at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_International_Anime_Fair" title="Tokyo International Anime Fair">Tokyo International Anime Fair</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Animage" title="Animage">Animage</a></i> Anime Grand Prix, and <a href="/wiki/Animation_Kobe" title="Animation Kobe">Animation Kobe</a> event. Critics have praised the series for its large audience appeal as well as the cross conflicts shown among the main characters and the moral questions presented.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Code_Geass_characters" title="List of Code Geass characters">List of Code Geass characters</a></div>
<p>The story is set in an <a href="/wiki/Parallel_universe_(fiction)" title="Parallel universe (fiction)">alternative timeline</a> where the world has become split into three <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a>: the Holy Britannian Empire (the Americas; also called Britannia), the Chinese Federation (Asia), and the European Union (Europe and Africa; previously known as the Euro-Universe. Also known as Europa United in <i>Akito the Exiled</i>). The story takes place after the Holy Britannian Empire's conquest of Japan on August 10, 2010 a.t.b., by means of Britannia's newest weapon, the "Autonomous Armored Knight", or "Knightmare Frame". In turn, Britannia effectively strips Japan and its citizens of all rights and freedoms and renames the country Area 11 with its citizens referred to as Elevens.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lelouch_vi_Britannia" title="Lelouch vi Britannia">Lelouch vi Britannia</a> is an exiled Britannian prince who was sent as a bargaining tool to Japan, along with his sister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nunnally_vi_Britannia" title="Nunnally vi Britannia">Nunnally vi Britannia</a>, by his father, Emperor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_zi_Britannia" title="Charles zi Britannia">Charles zi Britannia</a>, after his mother, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marianne_vi_Britannia" title="Marianne vi Britannia">Marianne vi Britannia</a>, was killed. Nunnally witnessed the murder of her mother Marianne, which caused her to lose both her sight and ability to walk. This makes it difficult for Lelouch because he must take care of her while on the run in Japan during the war. After the war in the ruins of a Japanese city he then vows to his Japanese friend <a href="/wiki/Suzaku_Kururugi" title="Suzaku Kururugi">Suzaku Kururugi</a> that he will one day obliterate Britannia.</p>
<p>Seven years later, Lelouch, now a popular yet withdrawn student at Ashford Academy by the name of Lelouch Lamperouge, gets caught up in a terrorist attack and finds a girl called <a href="/wiki/C.C._(Code_Geass)" title="C.C. (Code Geass)">C.C.</a> (C2), who saves Lelouch's life from the Britannian Royal Guard, by making a contract with him that grants Lelouch a power known as Geass <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ギアス</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Giasu</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>. This power, also known as the "Power of Kings" <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">王の力</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Ō no Chikara</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, allows him to command anyone to do whatever he wants, whether bending their will to live, fight, or die on his behalf –though only once and only through direct eye contact. Lelouch decides to put his Geass to use and find the person who killed his mother, destroy the Britannian Empire, and to create a better world where Nunnally can live happily. In the process, Lelouch becomes Zero, a masked vigilante and the leader of the resistance movement known as The Black Knights, gaining popularity and support among the Japanese on his way towards the rebellion of Britannia. However, this does not come without a cost. Caught up in a conflict where he does not know the full extent of his powers, Lelouch will have to battle Suzaku, a resistance member named <a href="/wiki/Kallen_Stadtfeld" title="Kallen Stadtfeld">Kallen Stadtfeld</a>, the strongest army in the world, his own half-siblings, and many others in a battle that will forever change the world.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Code Geass</i> began as a concept developed at Sunrise by <a href="/wiki/Ichir%C5%8D_%C5%8Ckouchi" title="Ichirō Ōkouchi">Ichirō Ōkouchi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gor%C5%8D_Taniguchi" title="Gorō Taniguchi">Gorō Taniguchi</a>, who proposed it to producer Yoshitaka Kawaguchi. Kawaguchi had previously approached Okouchi and Taniguchi during the production of <i><a href="/wiki/Planetes" title="Planetes">Planetes</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview-4">[4]</a></sup> The basic idea for the plot consisted of a "hero" who led a secret organization, which was later developed into a conflict between two characters with different values and who belonged to the same military unit, who eventually became <a href="/wiki/Lelouch_Lamperouge" title="Lelouch Lamperouge">Lelouch Lamperouge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suzaku_Kururugi" title="Suzaku Kururugi">Suzaku Kururugi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>During these initial planning stages, Kawaguchi also contacted the noted <a href="/wiki/Mangaka" title="Mangaka">manga artist</a> group <a href="/wiki/Clamp_(manga_artists)" title="Clamp (manga artists)">Clamp</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview-4">[4]</a></sup> This was the first time Clamp had ever been requested to design the characters of an anime series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup> Clamp signed onto the project early during these development stages and provided numerous ideas, which helped develop the series' setting and characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>While developing the character designs for Lelouch, the protagonist of the series, Clamp had originally conceived of his hair color as being white.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ageha_Ohkawa" title="Ageha Ohkawa">Ageha Ohkawa</a>, head writer at Clamp, said she had visualized him as being a character to which "everyone" could relate to as being "cool", literally, a "beauty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup> During these planning stages, Clamp and the Sunrise staff had discussed a number of possible inspirations for the characters, including <a href="/wiki/KinKi_Kids" title="KinKi Kids">KinKi Kids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tackey_%26_Tsubasa" title="Tackey &amp; Tsubasa">Tackey &amp; Tsubasa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup> They had wanted to create a "hit show," a series which would appeal to "everyone."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup> Lelouch's alter ego, Zero, was one of the earliest developed characters, with Ōkouchi having wanted a mask to be included as a part of the series, feeling it was necessary for it to be a Sunrise show, and Clamp wanting a unique design never prior seen in any Sunrise series (said mask was nicknamed "<a href="/wiki/Tulip" title="Tulip">tulip</a>" for its distinctive design).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The concept for the Geass may have been inspired by the Irish and Welsh legends of "Geis" or "Geas". A geis is a compulsion laid on someone to do or not do something. While the geis itself does not lie on any spectrum, the benefits or actions of it may be decidedly benevolent or malevolent. The concept fits in into the wider fictional world and its lore of British inspirations.</p>
<p>Clamp's finalized original character design art, illustrated by its lead artist <a href="/wiki/Mokona" title="Mokona">Mokona</a>, was subsequently converted into animation character designs for the series by Sunrise's character designer <a href="/wiki/Takahiro_Kimura" title="Takahiro Kimura">Takahiro Kimura</a>, who had previously spent "every day" analyzing Clamp's art and style from their artbooks and manga series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup> In working on the animation character designs, he focused on designing them so as to enable the series' other animators to apply them without deviating from Clamp's original art style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-.C5.8Dkawa-interview-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The music for the series was composed by <a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dtar%C5%8D_Nakagawa" title="Kōtarō Nakagawa">Kōtarō Nakagawa</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hitomi_Kuroishi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hitomi Kuroishi (page does not exist)">Hitomi Kuroishi</a>, who had earlier worked with the series' core staff in <i>Planetes</i> and Taniguchi's earlier work <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gun_X_Sword" title="Gun X Sword">Gun X Sword</a></i>. In addition to the <a href="/wiki/Incidental_music" title="Incidental music">incidental music</a> featured in each episode, Kuroishi also composed numerous insert songs for the series, including "Stories", "Masquerade", "Alone", and "Innocent Days", which were each performed by Kuroishi herself, while "Picaresque" and "Callin'" were performed by the <a href="/wiki/Singer-songwriter" title="Singer-songwriter">singer-songwriter</a> <a href="/wiki/Mikio_Sakai" title="Mikio Sakai">Mikio Sakai</a>, who had also earlier worked with Nakagawa and Kuroishi in <i>Planetes</i>. The bands <a href="/wiki/Flow_(band)" title="Flow (band)">FLOW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ali_Project" title="Ali Project">Ali Project</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinn_(band)" title="Jinn (band)">Jinn</a>, <a href="/wiki/SunSet_Swish" title="SunSet Swish">SunSet Swish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Access_(group)" title="Access (group)">Access</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orange_Range" title="Orange Range">Orange Range</a> have provided songs for the opening and ending themes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-offsite-cd_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-offsite-cd-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flowwe-news_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-flowwe-news-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the series was being developed for broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Mainichi_Broadcasting_System" title="Mainichi Broadcasting System">Mainichi Broadcasting System</a>, it had been given the network's Saturday evening <a href="/wiki/Prime_time" title="Prime time">prime time</a> slot, which was later changed to a Thursday <a href="/wiki/Late_night_anime" title="Late night anime">late night time</a> slot. Due to this change, the overall outlook and some elements of the series were changed and further developed to suit the more mature, late night audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview-4">[4]</a></sup> The supernatural "Geass" ability finally came into the show at this point and was first conceived as a special power granted by an "angel" to the main characters, though this last part was also modified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anime">Anime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Anime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Code_Geass:_Lelouch_of_the_Rebellion_episodes" title="List of Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion episodes">List of Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion episodes</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Code_Geass:_Lelouch_of_the_Rebellion_R2_episodes" title="List of Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion R2 episodes">List of Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion R2 episodes</a></div>
<p><i>Code Geass</i> officially premiered on the Mainichi Broadcasting System (MBS) television station at 25:25 on October 5, 2006 (01:25 <a href="/wiki/Japan_Standard_Time" title="Japan Standard Time">JST</a> on October 6, 2006). Its <a href="/wiki/Satellite_television" title="Satellite television">satellite television</a> premiere across Japan on <a href="/wiki/Animax" title="Animax">Animax</a> was on November 7, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moonphase_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-moonphase-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Upon the airing of the first 23 episodes, the series went on hiatus on March 29, 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moonphase_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-moonphase-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taniguchi-interview_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-taniguchi-interview-10">[10]</a></sup> and completed broadcast of the first series with a contiguous one-hour broadcast of episodes 24 and 25 at 26:25 on Saturday, July 28, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The immense popularity of <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion</i> followed with the development of its sequel, <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion R2</i>, which was first announced on the March 2007 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Newtype" title="Newtype">Newtype</a></i> and later confirmed by Sunrise producer Yoshitaka Kawaguchi on the series' official staff blog on March 9, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-random-geass_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-random-geass-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blog-sequel_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-blog-sequel-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion R2</i> premiered on all Japan News Network (JNN) member stations (like MBS and TBS) on April 6, 2008, in the primetime anime timeslot, with the timeslot changing from 18:00 JST on Saturdays to 17:00 JST on Sundays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moonphase-nt_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-moonphase-nt-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tbs-move_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-tbs-move-15">[15]</a></sup> Prior to the series' television broadcast, three private preview screenings of episode 1 were held on March 15 and March 16 in <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> respectively, which was attended by the series' Japanese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seiy%C5%AB" title="Seiyū">voice actors</a> as well as a pool of 3800 randomly selected applicants. On April 15, 2008, at 17:00 <a href="/wiki/Japan_Standard_Time" title="Japan Standard Time">JST</a>, the last 6 minutes of the then unaired third episode was accidentally posted onto the Internet due to an error by <a href="/wiki/Bandai_Channel" title="Bandai Channel">Bandai Channel</a>, Bandai's online broadcast channel and the series online distributor, in the midst of testing a system preventing illegal online uploads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official-site-statement_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-official-site-statement-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Revival/Resurrection R3</i> was announced on November 27, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Code Geass: The Miraculous Birthday</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反逆のルルーシュ キセキの誕生日</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Kiseki no Tanjōbi</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> picture drama was based on a live event held in Tokyo, Japan on Lelouch's birthday.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Another OVA anime titled <i>Code Geass: Nunnally in Wonderland</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反逆のルルーシュ： ナナリーinワンダーランド</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu Hangyaku no Rurūshu: Nanarī in wandārando</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> was announced and revealed through the anime's official website. <a href="/wiki/Takahiro_Kimura" title="Takahiro Kimura">Takahiro Kimura</a> will do the character designs of the series. Makoto Baba is assigned as the director of the OVA while episode scriptwriter Yuuichi Nomura and music composer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kotaro_Nakagawa" title="Kotaro Nakagawa">Kotaro Nakagawa</a> will return for the said project. In the story, Lelouch makes the ultimate use of his Geass for his little sister Nunnally, who loves Alice in Wonderland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a> was released by <a href="/wiki/Bandai_Visual" title="Bandai Visual">Bandai Visual</a> on July 27, 2012 with English subtitles and bundled with a 40 page picture book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Akito_the_Exiled">Akito the Exiled</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Akito the Exiled">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The new series was first revealed on December 5, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In April 2010, it was officially revealed that a new <i>Code Geass</i> side story anime called <i>Code Geass: Akito the Exiled</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 亡国のアキト</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Bōkoku no Akito</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> would be directed by <a href="/wiki/Kazuki_Akane" title="Kazuki Akane">Kazuki Akane</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Vision_of_Escaflowne" title="The Vision of Escaflowne">The Vision of Escaflowne</a></i>). The side story is OVA series set in Europe during the Britannian invasion of the continent between <i>Lelouch of the Rebellion'</i>s two seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Originally intended to be released in four chapters, production of a fifth <i>Akito the Exiled</i> episode was announced after the Japanese debut of the third entry on May 2, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Along with the two seasons of the television series, the OVAs are licensed by <a href="/wiki/Funimation" title="Funimation">Funimation</a>. In January 2016, <a href="/wiki/Manga_Entertainment" title="Manga Entertainment">Manga Entertainment</a>, who licensed the series in the UK, listed that they will release the first two episodes on Blu-Ray with an English dub on December 5, 2016 later changing the date to April 10, 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madman_Entertainment" title="Madman Entertainment">Madman Entertainment</a> has also released the first three episodes on DVD. Funimation announced it will release the series in early 2017. The picture drama has been released in only Japan and Italy.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_licensing">International licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: International licensing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Both seasons of <i>Code Geass</i> have been licensed for release in the United States by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bandai_Entertainment" title="Bandai Entertainment">Bandai Entertainment</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and the first season began airing on <a href="/wiki/Cartoon_Network" title="Cartoon Network">Cartoon Network</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Adult_Swim" title="Adult Swim">Adult Swim</a> programming block in the U.S. on April 27, 2008; the second began airing on November 2, immediately following the first season, both viewable in English on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adult_Swim_Video" title="Adult Swim Video">Adult Swim Video</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The series finale premiered on June 7, 2009, ending the second season and the rest of the story. On April 23, 2010, Adult Swim's rights to this series expired.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Following the closure of Bandai Entertainment in 2012, <a href="/wiki/Sunrise_(company)" title="Sunrise (company)">Sunrise</a> announced at their official panel during <a href="/wiki/Otakon" title="Otakon">Otakon</a> 2013 that <a href="/wiki/Funimation" title="Funimation">Funimation</a> has rescued both seasons of Code Geass and in addition licensed <i>Akito the Exiled</i>, along with a handful of other former Bandai Entertainment titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia and New Zealand, the series is sub-licensed to <a href="/wiki/Madman_Entertainment" title="Madman Entertainment">Madman Entertainment</a> by Bandai Entertainment USA,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and began airing on Australian channel <a href="/wiki/ABC2" title="ABC2">ABC2</a> from January 19, 2009.</p>
<p>In the Philippines, the first season of Code Geass premiered on November 10, 2008, weekday nights at 7:30pm <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Standard_Time" title="Philippine Standard Time">PST</a> and ended on December 15, 2008 through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associated_Broadcasting_Company" title="Associated Broadcasting Company">TV5</a>, while season 2 premiered on May 4, 2009 and ended on June 5, 2009, weekday nights at 6:00pm <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Standard_Time" title="Philippine Standard Time">PST</a> with a weekend afternoon recap of the week's episodes also on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associated_Broadcasting_Company" title="Associated Broadcasting Company">TV5</a>. Despite the poor ratings it attained due to competition with local TV newscasts and prime time soaps, the series was able to gain a huge following and became one of the most talked-about anime series in the country during its run. Code Geass had its Philippine cable premiere on July 27, 2010 through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hero_TV" title="Hero TV">Hero TV</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, the first season aired from September 23, 2009 to February 25, 2010 on <a href="/wiki/Rai_4" title="Rai 4">Rai 4</a>, while season 2 was broadcast on Rai 4 from March 4, 2010 to August 12, 2010; both seasons were broadcast at about 11:10 pm.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manga">Manga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Manga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Code_Geass_chapters" title="List of Code Geass chapters">List of Code Geass chapters</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kadokawa_Shoten" title="Kadokawa Shoten">Kadokawa Shoten</a> has published four separate manga adaptations, each containing an alternate storyline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-book-28">[28]</a></sup> The first four of the manga series have been licensed for an <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> release in North America by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bandai_Entertainment" title="Bandai Entertainment">Bandai Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYAF_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYAF-29">[29]</a></sup> The first, <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion</i>, by Majiko~! and originally serialized <i><a href="/wiki/Monthly_Asuka" title="Monthly Asuka">Monthly Asuka</a></i>, focused on the protagonist of the series, <a href="/wiki/Lelouch_Lamperouge" title="Lelouch Lamperouge">Lelouch Lamperouge</a>, with few differences from the anime's basic storyline. The most noticeable difference from the anime version is the absence of the Knightmare frames. Its chapters were collected in eight <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes released from December 26, 2008 to March 26, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstrebellion_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstrebellion-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lastrebellion_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-lastrebellion-31">[31]</a></sup> Bandai's English adaptation of the series was published from July 29, 2008<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-engfirst.1_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-engfirst.1-32">[32]</a></sup> to February 15, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lastengrebellion_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-lastengrebellion-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second manga is <i>Code Geass: Suzaku of the Counterattack</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反攻のスザク</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Hankō no Suzaku</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>. It was written by Atsuro Yomino and serialized in <i>Beans A</i> magazine. It focuses on the character <a href="/wiki/Suzaku_Kururugi" title="Suzaku Kururugi">Suzaku Kururugi</a> in an alternate reality, where he fights against the criminal organization known as the Black Knights. It was released in two volumes on June 26, 2007 and September 26, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstsuzaku_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstsuzaku-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secsuzaku_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-secsuzaku-35">[35]</a></sup> The first English volume was released on January 6, 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstengsuzaku_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstengsuzaku-36">[36]</a></sup> and the second followed it on October 13, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secondengsuzaku_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-secondengsuzaku-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Code Geass: Nightmare of Nunnally</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス ナイトメア・オブ・ナナリー</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu Naitomea Obu Nanarī</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, serialized in <i><a href="/wiki/Comp_Ace" title="Comp Ace">Comp Ace</a></i> and written by Tomomasa Takuma, focuses on Lelouch's sister, <a href="/wiki/Nunnally_Lamperouge" title="Nunnally Lamperouge">Nunnally Lamperouge</a> who goes into searching her missing brother when her health is restored by an entity named Nemo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-book-28">[28]</a></sup> It was published in five volumes from June 26, 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstnanually_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstnanually-38">[38]</a></sup> to April 25, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lastnunnally_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-lastnunnally-39">[39]</a></sup> The English volumes were published from June 9, 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-engfirstnanually_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-engfirstnanually-40">[40]</a></sup> to March 23, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lastengnunnally_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-lastengnunnally-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>A fourth manga adaptation, <i>Code Geass: Tales of an Alternate Shogunate</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">幕末異聞録 コードギアス 反逆のルルーシュ</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Bakumatsu Ibun Roku Kōdo Giasu Hangyaku no Rurūshu</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, was serialized in <a href="/wiki/Kerokero_Ace" title="Kerokero Ace">Kerokero Ace</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Set in an alternate 1853, Lelouch is the commander of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shogunate" title="Shogunate">Shogunate</a>'s military counterinsurgence brigade known as the <a href="/wiki/Shinsengumi" title="Shinsengumi">Shinsengumi</a>, which fights the <a href="/wiki/Shishi_(organization)" title="Shishi (organization)">Black Revolutionaries</a>, a rebel group led by a masked individual known as Rei. It was released on a single volume on October 25, 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstalter_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstalter-42">[42]</a></sup> while the English version was published on May 10, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-engalter_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-engalter-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late 2009, Bandai announced a new project greenlit for 2010. A manga, titled <i>Code Geass: Renya of Darkness</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 漆黒の連夜</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Shikkoku no Renya</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, is the first product announced. The story takes place in the same official <i>Code Geass</i> history as the anime, but in a different era with the anime director <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goro_Taniguchi" title="Goro Taniguchi">Goro Taniguchi</a> scripting the story. The title character, Renya, is a 17-year-old boy who encounters a mysterious, perpetually young witch named "Reifū C.C.", who has appeared in Japan's historical Edo era to seek a new partner for a covenant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> It began publication in the May 2010 issue of <i>Shōnen Ace</i>. Bandai Entertainment announced that it will publish the manga in English as with the other adaptions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> On January 2, 2012 as a part of Bandai Entertainment's announced restructuring, they have since, among other titles, revoked publishing of Code Geass: Renya of Darkness for English release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Code Geass spinoff Oz the Reflection takes place between the first and second seasons of the TV anime and is told from two perspectives. The photo story in Hobby Japan centers around Orpheus Zevon, a young terrorist with the Knightmare Frame Byakuen who is in pursuit of his lover's killer. The manga in Newtype Ace revolves around Oldrin Zevon, a girl in the Britannia Empire's anti-terrorist unit Glinda Knights who pilots the Knightmare Frame Lancelot Grail. The story of Oz the Reflection and Akito the Exiled takes place at the same time in between season 1 and 2 of the TV series.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CDs">CDs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: CDs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The series has been adapted into a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_CD" title="Drama CD">drama CDs</a>, called <i>Sound Episodes</i>, the first of which was released in Japan in April 2007 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victor_Entertainment" title="Victor Entertainment">Victor Entertainment</a>, with new volumes released monthly. Written by many of the same writers as the series, these episodes are set between episodes and feature theme songs performed by the series' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seiy%C5%AB" title="Seiyū">voice actors</a>. They have also been available online on a limited streaming basis on the Japanese internet website Biglobe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In total, twelve drama CDs have been released. The first six, released between April 25, 2007 and September 27, 2007 cover the first season of the series, and the other six focusing on the second season.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtrack">Soundtrack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Soundtrack">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The music for the series, composed by <a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dtar%C5%8D_Nakagawa" title="Kōtarō Nakagawa">Kōtarō Nakagawa</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hitomi_Kuroishi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hitomi Kuroishi (page does not exist)">Hitomi Kuroishi</a>, has been released across two original soundtracks produced by Yoshimoto Ishikawa and released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victor_Entertainment" title="Victor Entertainment">Victor Entertainment</a>. The first was released in Japan on December 20, 2006, and the second on March 24, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-offsite-cd_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-offsite-cd-6">[6]</a></sup> The covers and jackets for both soundtracks were illustrated by <a href="/wiki/Takahiro_Kimura" title="Takahiro Kimura">Takahiro Kimura</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-offsite-cd_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-offsite-cd-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Light_novels">Light novels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Light novels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Code_Geass_light_novels" title="List of Code Geass light novels">List of Code Geass light novels</a></div>
<p><i>Code Geass</i> has been additionally novelized into a series of <a href="/wiki/Light_novel" title="Light novel">light novels</a>. First serialized in <a href="/wiki/Kadokawa_Shoten" title="Kadokawa Shoten">Kadokawa Shoten</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sneaker" title="The Sneaker">The Sneaker</a></i> magazine, they are divided into two separate series corresponding with the series two seasons. The first series, <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion</i>, spanned five volumes with the first, labelled as volume 0, released in Japan on April 28, 2007 and the last on March 1, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-first-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-last_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-last-48">[48]</a></sup> All five volumes in the first series of novels have been released in English by <a href="/wiki/Bandai_Visual" title="Bandai Visual">Bandai Visual</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYAF_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYAF-29">[29]</a></sup> The first volume was released on November 2008 and the last one on February 23, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-last_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-last-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-engfirst.0_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-engfirst.0-49">[49]</a></sup> The first novel acts as a prologue, focusing on how Lelouch befriended <a href="/wiki/Suzaku_Kururugi" title="Suzaku Kururugi">Suzaku Kururugi</a>, when the former prince and his sister <a href="/wiki/Nunnally_Lamperouge" title="Nunnally Lamperouge">Nunnally Lamperouge</a> were sent to Japan as political hostages.</p>
<p>The second novel series, <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion R2</i>, covers the second season of the anime series in which Lelouch continues his battle against the Britannian Empire. It was released in four volumes from June 1, 2008 to March 1, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstrtwo_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstrtwo-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lastrtwo_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-lastrtwo-51">[51]</a></sup> A single volume side story novel, <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion Red Tracks</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反逆のルルーシュ 朱の軌跡</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Hangyaku no Rurūshu Shu no Kiseki</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> was released on April 1, 2008 in Japan. It focuses on the life of teenager girl <a href="/wiki/Kallen_Stadtfeld" title="Kallen Stadtfeld">Kallen Stadtfeld</a> who becomes a soldier from the organization the Black Knights under Lelouch's leadership to defeat Britannia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redtracks_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-redtracks-52">[52]</a></sup> On January 3, 2012, the English publication of the light novel adaptation of R2 had been announced as cancelled as part of Bandai Entertainment's planned restructuring which had been announced the day before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_News_Network_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_News_Network-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The series was also slated to be adapted into a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_games" title="Video games">video games</a>, developed for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-game_RPG_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-game_RPG-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> platforms, which was published by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namco_Bandai" title="Namco Bandai">Namco Bandai Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendo_wii_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-nintendo_wii-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> All three games have been available in only Japanese, although an incomplete <a href="/wiki/Unofficial_patch" title="Unofficial patch">unofficial patch</a> for the Nintendo DS game exists on the internet that partially translates the game into English.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> platform is cancelled for unknown reason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendo_wii_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendo_wii-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The official website for the first Nintendo DS game launched on July 16, 2007, with the game being released a few months later on October 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>A second game, titled <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion Lost Colors</i> was developed for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a>, and released in Japan on March 27, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Visual_novel" title="Visual novel">visual novel</a> game which follows a new protagonist named Rai <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ライ</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, who suffers from amnesia. He has a Geass ability similar to <a href="/wiki/Lelouch_Lamperouge" title="Lelouch Lamperouge">Lelouch</a>'s, but activated by voice.</p>
<p>The third game for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> is a collection of minigames featuring <a href="/wiki/Super_deformed" title="Super deformed">super deformed</a> forms of the characters. The player moves along a board through dice rolls, landing on different spots to activate minigames. The minigames are parody-style events with multiple genres. These include helping Jeremiah grow oranges, racing against C.C. and Shirley in swimming, and a sidescrolling beat-em-up featuring Kallen in Guren-like armor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><i>Code Geass R2</i> is slated to appear in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/From_Software" title="From Software">From Software</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Demon%27s_Souls" title="Demon's Souls">Demon's Souls</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Armored_Core" title="Armored Core">Armored Core</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Banpresto" title="Banpresto">Banpresto</a>'s <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> exclusive <a href="/wiki/Mecha" title="Mecha">mecha</a> action game <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Another_Century%27s_Episode_R" title="Another Century's Episode R">Another Century's Episode R</a></i>, released in Japan in August 2010 and in which both versions of Suzaku's Lancelot, Lelouch's Shinkiro, both versions of Kallen's Guren, and C.C.'s Akatsuki are playable. A fourth installment of the ACE franchise for the PlayStation Portable, <a href="/wiki/Another_Century%27s_Episode_Portable" title="Another Century's Episode Portable">Another Century's Episode Portable</a>, will include Suzaku's Lancelot Albion and Lelouch/Zero's Shinkiro.</p>
<p><i>Code Geass</i> characters have appeared as costumes in the Japanese version of the PlayStation 3 game, <a href="/wiki/Tales_of_Graces" title="Tales of Graces">Tales of Graces F</a>. These characters are Zero, Suzaku, C.C. and Kallen. These costumes were never released from the US version for unknown reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artbooks">Artbooks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Artbooks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two artbooks featuring illustrations of the series, <i>Code Geass Graphics Zero</i> (<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/4048540793">ISBN 4048540793</a>) and <i>Code Geass Graphics Ashford</i> (<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/4048540807">ISBN 4048540807</a>), have been published in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-book-28">[28]</a></sup> Coinciding with the release of the second season of <i>Code Geass</i> was the publication of another artbook, <i>Code Geass – Lelouch of the Rebellion illustrations Rebels</i> (<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/4048541692">ISBN 4048541692</a>), which featured 134 art pieces of the first season. Another 95 page artbook titled <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion – The Complete Artbook</i> (<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9784048541183">ISBN 9784048541183</a>) has also been published. Finally, CLAMP, the well-known manga artist team who did the designs for Code Geass, put out their own artbook, entitled Code Geass x CLAMP: Mutuality.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_radio_broadcasts">Internet radio broadcasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Internet radio broadcasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Code Geass" has also been adapted into a series of weekly <a href="/wiki/Internet_radio" title="Internet radio">internet radio</a> broadcasts, which were streamed online on the BEAT☆Net Radio! portal, the first of which, <i>Code Geass: The Rebellion Diary</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反逆日記</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu: Hangyaku Nikki</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, began streaming from October 6, 2006. It featured <a href="/wiki/Sayaka_Ohara" title="Sayaka Ohara">Sayaka Ohara</a> (voice actor of Milly Ashford) and <a href="/wiki/Satomi_Arai" title="Satomi Arai">Satomi Arai</a> (voice actor of Sayoko Shinazaki). The second, <i>Code Geass – Mountains of the Rebellion</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス 反逆の山々</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu Hangyaku no Yamayama</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, was first streamed on December 12, 2006, and were hosted by <a href="/wiki/Jun_Fukuyama" title="Jun Fukuyama">Jun Fukuyama</a> (voice actor of Lelouch) and <a href="/wiki/Noriaki_Sugiyama" title="Noriaki Sugiyama">Noriaki Sugiyama</a> (voice actor of Rivalz). During <i>R2</i>, a new show named <i>Code Geass – LuluKuru Station</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">コードギアス ルルクルステーション</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kōdo Giasu Rurukuru Suteishōn</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> was streamed, hosted by Fukuyama and <a href="/wiki/Takahiro_Sakurai" title="Takahiro Sakurai">Takahiro Sakurai</a> (voice actor of Suzaku).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Code Geass</i> received critical acclaim since its release. Despite the wide variety of mecha designed and prominently featuring in the show, fans of <i>Code Geass</i> are of a wide variety and not always attracted purely to the Knightmare combat scenes. <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">Anime News Network</a>'s columnist Todd Ciolek attributes the soaring popularity of <i>Code Geass</i> to "the series hitting every important fan sector", with the audience appeal points ranging from a "complex cast of characters and a fast-paced story, told with Goro Taniguchi's capable direction" for "general-interest fans" to "pretty and just-a-little-broken heroes" for "<a href="/wiki/Yaoi" title="Yaoi">yaoi</a>-buying female fans".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_TC_XB_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_TC_XB-61">[61]</a></sup> Carl Kimlinger also finds that the series "has the skill and energy to carry viewers over the top with it, where they can spend a pleasurable few hours reveling in its melodramatic charms."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> He also adds that Taniguchi "executes the excesses of his series with care, skillfully intercutting events as Lelouch's plans come together (or fall apart) and using kinetic mecha combat".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carlo Santos of Anime News Network wrote that the franchise "in a way, [...] reflects the <a href="/wiki/Malaise" title="Malaise">malaise</a> of a generation: the realization that old, rich, powerful people have screwed up the world and that the young are helpless to do anything about it". According to him, Lelouch's actions exemplify the wish to see problems like "<a href="/wiki/Economic_collapse" title="Economic collapse">economic collapse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Class_conflict" title="Class conflict">class conflict</a>, political instability, <a href="/wiki/Extremism" title="Extremism">radical extremism</a>" solved by "Zero's <a href="/wiki/Vigilante" title="Vigilante">vigilante</a> methods" but Santos expresses doubt in such an approach and concludes that "the series is at its best when raising questions rather than offering a final solution".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_G1_rev_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_G1_rev-64">[64]</a></sup> T.H.E.M. Anime Reviewer Dallas Marshall gave the series 4 out of 5 stars, stating "A melodramatic piece of science fiction that has more than enough going for it in terms of action and visuals but tends to go overboard with its emotionalism. If this minor flaw can be overlooked, there is an epic story to be told with a rather intriguing main character at the helm. Take away one star if that minor 'flaw' cannot be ignored."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_and_accolades">Sales and accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Code_Geass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sales and accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When the first episode was shown during a special test screening, which was attended by Ōkawa, other members of the series' staff, as well as several journalists and other media-related personnel in response to the hype surrounding the series' upcoming release, the audience fell into immediate silence after it ended, followed by "tremendous applause."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.8Dkouchi-interview-4">[4]</a></sup> By August 2008, over 900,000 <i>Code Geass</i> discs had been sold in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Reportedly, Bandai Visual shipped over one million DVD and Blu-ray Discs related to the <i>Code Geass</i> franchise by November 2008, placing it among the most popular contemporary anime series in both Japan and North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_HF_OST2_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_HF_OST2-67">[67]</a></sup> During 2008, the first volume from <i>R2</i> was the fourth bestselling anime DVD and Blu-ray Disc in Japan according to <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since its premiere, <i>Code Geass: Lelouch of the Rebellion</i> has collected numerous awards and accolades. At the sixth annual Tokyo Anime Awards held at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_International_Anime_Fair" title="Tokyo International Anime Fair">Tokyo International Anime Fair</a>, <i>Code Geass</i> won the best TV anime series award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fair_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-fair-69">[69]</a></sup> The second season also got the award of "Best Screenplay" in the 2009 Tokyo Anime Fair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In noted Japanese anime magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Animage" title="Animage">Animage</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 29th Annual Anime Grand Prix, <i>Code Geass</i> won the most popular series award, with <a href="/wiki/Lelouch_Lamperouge" title="Lelouch Lamperouge">Lelouch Lamperouge</a> also being chosen as the most popular male character and "Colors" being chosen as the most popular song<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. In the 30th Annual Anime Grand Prix, Lelouch won first place again and <a href="/wiki/C.C._(Code_Geass)" title="C.C. (Code Geass)">C.C.</a> was voted most popular female character<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. At the first <a href="/wiki/Seiyu_Awards" title="Seiyu Awards">Seiyu Awards</a> held in 2007, <a href="/wiki/Jun_Fukuyama" title="Jun Fukuyama">Jun Fukuyama</a> won the award for best actor in a leading role for his performance as Lelouch Lamperouge in the series, while <a href="/wiki/Ami_Koshimizu" title="Ami Koshimizu">Ami Koshimizu</a> won the award for best actress in a supporting role for her performance as <a href="/wiki/Kallen_Stadtfeld" title="Kallen Stadtfeld">Kallen Stadtfeld</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Furthermore, <i>Code Geass</i> won the award for Best TV Animation at the twelfth <a href="/wiki/Animation_Kobe" title="Animation Kobe">Animation Kobe</a> event, held annually in <a href="/wiki/Kobe" title="Kobe">Kobe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hy%C5%8Dgo_Prefecture" title="Hyōgo Prefecture">Hyōgo Prefecture</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kobe_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-kobe-72">[72]</a></sup> with <i>R2</i> taking the award in the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In the 2009, <a href="/wiki/Seiun_Award" title="Seiun Award">Seiun Award</a>, <i>Code Geass R2</i> was a nominee in the category "Best Media Award".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Doroku (2002-2008)</th>
